[4/23/2011 9:08:08 PM] gawrije:  No machan....it's not true. I agree that no country is perfect and no country is a utopia. Every so called democratic countries has their share of problems. But what differs is the 'degree to which democracy is practiced' in these countries as opposed to our country. Not in every country journalists/people get white-vanned for speaking in public. Not in every country you can overpower people with thugs and goons like ours. I can go on and on with so many examples but you know them as well as I do since we all come from the same place. 

You ask where there is un-hyped media. Agreed. Nowhere. But here, media channels still criticize Republicans and Democrats alike for what it's worth. Surely there are biases. But still they allow some space for opposing opinions. Do we see that in our state media? We can just dream of it right? :)

This link is the epitome of democracy for me. I wonder we'll ever see something like this in our countries. 

http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=DvdfO0lq4rQ

Now don't go all and say that I've become american or something. But we should appreciate things for what it is. 

BTW, I found the source for your previous comment. Again, I wonder if this is again evidence of how our media deceives our own people.

http://adaderana.lk/news.php?nid=12890

This says the top ten in the online poll didn't make it to the final 100 list but in fact there are three who have gone on to the final list. Also this says that Wael Ghonim is selected as the most influential person in the world according to TIME. But I don't see any evidence to the fact that TIME has done any ordering in this list. There's no numbered list which gives me the indication that they haven't made an effort to rank who is the most influential rather than putting forward the 100 people in no-specific-order. 

(PS: I don't give a damn about the TIME 100 list but just that it brought up so much hype among our people just interests me) :)
